    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer5364552691337457782">Described as "The best book as far as the attainment of happiness goes." by readersfavorite.com, Lucky Go Happy is an amusing, modern-day fable for adults and teens alike. <br/> <br/>Readers wanting to make happiness happen for themselves or those around them will gain insight into being happier - and being happy more often.<br/><br/>Happiness, emotions and positive psychology are abstract co</span>
  <span id="freeText5364552691337457782" style="display:none">Described as "The best book as far as the attainment of happiness goes." by readersfavorite.com, Lucky Go Happy is an amusing, modern-day fable for adults and teens alike. <br /> <br />Readers wanting to make happiness happen for themselves or those around them will gain insight into being happier - and being happy more often.<br /><br />Happiness, emotions and positive psychology are abstract concepts that are generally difficult to explain and understand.<br /><br />Adopting a unique approach, Lucky Go Happy unpacks these abstract concepts using the odd elementary graph and image, which when conveyed to readers through a fable makes for an informative and entertaining read for young and old.<br /><br />Lucky Go Happy follows the adventures of Lucky the Rat who has been sent into the African Bush by King Lion, to discover what makes other animals happy.<br /><br />Through various encounters with remarkable characters, Lucky captures some reviving new takes on happiness which he has to present to King Lion in a report before the next rainy season. King Lion hopes to regain his own happiness after reading the report.<br /><br />Lucky Go Happy will:<br /><br />- demonstrate how we lose more than 70 percent of potential happy time by living for weekends only<br />- explain how contentment can yield the same amount of happiness as ecstasy<br />- provide concrete proof that money can never - and will never - make us happy<br />- highlight why it is absolutely essential to be unhappy at times-<br />- illustrate why a midlife crisis happens<br />- show that happiness is not around the next corner; it is here and now,<br />- andhelp you understand how happiness works.<br /><br />Rather than waiting for happiness, you can make it happen for yourself and for those around you!<br /><br />Visit <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.luckygohappybook.com">www.luckygohappybook.com</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="5364552691337457782" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>

<div id="review_1410884807" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1410884807" />
    <a title="Sheila" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2039269-sheila"><img alt="Sheila" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1463428927p2/2039269.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1410884807?book_show_action=true">Oct 07, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sheila" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sheila" href="/user/show/2039269-sheila">Sheila</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2039269-sheila?shelf=animals">animals</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2039269-sheila?shelf=cultural">cultural</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2039269-sheila?shelf=current_issues">current_issues</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2039269-sheila?shelf=humor">humor</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2039269-sheila?shelf=self-help">self-help</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1410884807" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11492203689523887393">With chapters that separately cover their own pieces of the “complex puzzle” which is happiness, Paul Van Der Merwe offers a story-book on happiness that might equally be read by random dipping as by sequential reading—rather like happiness itself. Parable or fable, these tales read smoothly and “happily” while teaching wise lessons through humor and animal interest. I read them sequentially, laughed out loud on occasion, and thoroughly enjoyed those stings in rat-like tails—Lucky being a rat (a</span>
  <span id="freeText11492203689523887393" style="display:none">With chapters that separately cover their own pieces of the “complex puzzle” which is happiness, Paul Van Der Merwe offers a story-book on happiness that might equally be read by random dipping as by sequential reading—rather like happiness itself. Parable or fable, these tales read smoothly and “happily” while teaching wise lessons through humor and animal interest. I read them sequentially, laughed out loud on occasion, and thoroughly enjoyed those stings in rat-like tails—Lucky being a rat (and a math teacher, no less!) in a Bushveld world of lions, elephants and more.<br /><br />Based on a theory that all our actions are aimed at increasing happiness, Lucky is sent to investigate the stories of other animals. Pleasing humor invites the reader into each tale, and intriguing situations transport modern life into the world of animals, as creatures tell what they’ve learned of happiness. The stories are offered with an unforced sense of fable, making this a really enjoyable read.<br /><br />My favorite story just might be the marketing executive hyena, creating “unhappiness while also supplying the fix.” “Be happy with the fur you live in” might be the wisest advice to un-furred humans as well as to Lucky the rat. And my favorite lesson? Well, I’m just going to check this review off my to-do list, plan next year’s vacation, and take life a little slower. I’m not sure happiness really is the only destination, but I do know I enjoyed this book. It’s even got (simple) graphs to appeal to the mathematician in me—after all, Lucky is a math teacher!<br /><br />Disclosure: I was given a free ecopy and I offer my honest review.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11492203689523887393" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText12431553031930406010" style="display:none">This is an absolutely delightful little book on happiness that has good advice on virtually every page. Mainly it dishes out advice on what to do to create more happiness in your own life, examples of others who have sought happiness from external stimuli and failed, as well as stories about what has been proven to work for scores of people (and animals). It’s a story, yet it incorporates advice and humor. It’s an adventure with reflection, thought and insight. I recommend this book to anyone who is trying to become more positive or simply wants to enjoy his or her life a bit more. </span>

<div id="review_1224101195" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1224101195" />
    <a title="Bob Rich" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1425635-bob-rich"><img alt="Bob Rich" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1391399306p2/1425635.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1224101195?book_show_action=true">Mar 10, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bob Rich" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bob Rich" href="/user/show/1425635-bob-rich">Bob Rich</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1224101195" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7968095923175210153">From Aesop’s Fables on, animal stories have often been used to teach deep lessons. As a father long ago, and now a professional grandfather, I have enjoyed many. Nor are they all for children -- think of Watership Down for example.<br/><br/>Paul has used this time-honoured device in a delightful way, to present the findings of Positive Psychology in what is supposedly a children’s book. As is often the case, adults will get more out of it than kids, although a bright 10 to 12 year old will benefit, not on</span>
  <span id="freeText7968095923175210153" style="display:none">From Aesop’s Fables on, animal stories have often been used to teach deep lessons. As a father long ago, and now a professional grandfather, I have enjoyed many. Nor are they all for children -- think of Watership Down for example.<br /><br />Paul has used this time-honoured device in a delightful way, to present the findings of Positive Psychology in what is supposedly a children’s book. As is often the case, adults will get more out of it than kids, although a bright 10 to 12 year old will benefit, not only learning about how to strive for a good life, but also being presented with some simple mathematical concepts in an enjoyable way.<br /><br />I love the twists of humour, like Vulture being a vegetarian greengrocer, or that HAPPINESSISNOWHERE	can be “happiness is nowhere” or “happiness is now here.”<br /><br />Paul has earned my particular approval for demonstrating with mathematical exactitude that money has nothing to do with happiness. This is done in several guises, each entertaining and easy to understand. And in our greedy, conflict-ridden age, it is nice to see the creatures of the Bushveld acting with decency, compassion, generosity and wisdom.<br /><br />I wish humans could follow them.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7968095923175210153" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Claire - The Coffeeholic Bookworm" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Claire - The Coffeeholic Bookworm" href="/user/show/19367448-claire---the-coffeeholic-bookworm">Claire - The Coffeeholic Bookworm</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1272211415" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13406824099450315206">This had been a highly entertaining and though-provoking book. At first glance, you'll think this is some kind of a Self-Help book teaching you how to find happiness. But, surprise, surprise! Lucky Go Happy isn't just your ordinary book. There is quite a story to it, a journey of sorts, on how a Lion King sent his friend, Lucky the Rat on a quest to finding real happiness. This book or fable has depth, heart and soul. <br/><br/>Lucky was fortunate to have met a number of animals, who in one way or another</span>
  <span id="freeText13406824099450315206" style="display:none">This had been a highly entertaining and though-provoking book. At first glance, you'll think this is some kind of a Self-Help book teaching you how to find happiness. But, surprise, surprise! Lucky Go Happy isn't just your ordinary book. There is quite a story to it, a journey of sorts, on how a Lion King sent his friend, Lucky the Rat on a quest to finding real happiness. This book or fable has depth, heart and soul. <br /><br />Lucky was fortunate to have met a number of animals, who in one way or another, have unknowingly taught the rat the reality of happines, how easily it is taken away from you, how it is often overlooked and taken for granted, and how it could be cultivated and earned in our everyday lives. The animals - Elephant, Baobab, the Panda, Buffalo, Rhinocerous, even the butterflies - had all shared their insights, experiences, lessons and opinions about the different kinds of happiness. <br /><br />Clearly, the author had researched thoroughly for this book. He meant for the readers not only to enjoy, but also to learn and meditate and contemplate. If we are forever looking for the happiness that will fulfill our lives, this book will definitely help us a lot!</span>
  <a data-text-id="13406824099450315206" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17094469-janice-spina?shelf=books-reviewed">books-reviewed</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1338135973" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6898979885935520411">Lucky Go Happy is a positive book reinforcing the need for all creatures to realize happiness in their lives. Lucky is a rat who is commissioned by lion to find out all he can about the state of happiness and its importance and meaning from other animals' perspective. Lucky travels far and wide and gathers all the material and evidence from other animals along the way. Each animal gives Lucky his take on what happiness means to him. Some animals supply graphs depicting their lives and results of</span>
  <span id="freeText6898979885935520411" style="display:none">Lucky Go Happy is a positive book reinforcing the need for all creatures to realize happiness in their lives. Lucky is a rat who is commissioned by lion to find out all he can about the state of happiness and its importance and meaning from other animals' perspective. Lucky travels far and wide and gathers all the material and evidence from other animals along the way. Each animal gives Lucky his take on what happiness means to him. Some animals supply graphs depicting their lives and results of whether they were happy and how they achieved this happiness.<br /><br />This is an upbeat story that will make the readers think long and hard about their lives and if they achieved happiness. If they have not then what they should do to obtain it. This story was written in a clever way by using animals instead of people. I was given this book in exchange for an honest review. I would recommend it to those readers who need direction in how to obtain a happy life.<br /><br /><br /></span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('JwkOVwbALQAaC4TvT8s6yuYC7eM3oLqTgMuXsGoTv7ug8jaP4LEAPrCdy0BbYYfJWgbfn5EGTxUXlfgJGw9u3A==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('IjIrQG8QgAHMy0vTLPcd7qFEu9GsPAxDv+nLPc3hoxWlyROYiWGtP2ZdBHw4XaDtHUCJrQqa+cUot6SEvP1ycg==')})
  }

        $('bookCover_29496453').observe('prototip:shown', function () {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('bookCover_29496453').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;
            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('bookCover_29496453').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

//]]>
</script>

</li>
</ul>
</div>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/6406273.Paul_Van_Der_Merwe">About Paul Van Der Merwe</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/6406273.Paul_Van_Der_Merwe"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1480095918p3/6406273.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer14508036251627523792">Paul van der Merwe is an author, engineer and a Guinness World Record holder.<br/><br/>Always looking for new and exciting ways to challenge the status quo, Paul launched his first book in the true sense of the word.<br/><br/>The book was strapped to a model rocket along with a space LEGO pilot and literally launched into the African sky.<br/><br/>Here is a link to the launch video:<br/><a>Video : Rocket Powered Book Launch</a><br/><br/>He spends h</span>
  <span id="freeText14508036251627523792" style="display:none">Paul van der Merwe is an author, engineer and a Guinness World Record holder.<br /><br />Always looking for new and exciting ways to challenge the status quo, Paul launched his first book in the true sense of the word.<br /><br />The book was strapped to a model rocket along with a space LEGO pilot and literally launched into the African sky.<br /><br />Here is a link to the launch video:<br /><a>Video : Rocket Powered Book Launch</a><br /><br />He spends his days working as an engineering manager for an engineering contractor that executes large capital projects for the international mining and minerals industry. He and his wife, Corlia, have two children and live in Pretoria, South Africa.<br /><br />Paul’s motivation for writing Lucky Go Happy is quite an interesting story:<br /><br />“During my first assignment as project engineer, I was responsible for executing the engineering design and drawings for the construction of a diamond processing plant, high up in the Maluti Mountains in the Kingdom of Lesotho.<br /><br />This was an extremely stressful period for me, and for the first time in my life I had problems falling asleep. In order not to think about work, I forced myself to have happy thoughts; hoping it would stop my mind from racing back to work.<br /><br />During these periods of being half-awake and half-asleep, the mind is extremely creative and this is where engineering (math actually) met psychology; fields that are generally poles apart. This odd marriage resulted in the formulation of some interesting perspectives on happiness, somewhere around 2am most mornings.<br /><br />My plan had backfired on me as I was now being kept awake formulating my theories on happiness.<br /><br />I captured my thoughts, in a note book that I kept under my bed, so I would remember them the next day. <br /><br />The number of notes and sketches grew, and eventually I had enough material to write Lucky Go Happy; allowing me to share my ideas with the world while also fulfilling my lifelong dream of publishing a book.”<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14508036251627523792" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
